## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Solid Mechanics / Materials Science
**Analysis**: This task models the constitutive relationship between stress, strain, and temperature, which is fundamental to continuum mechanics and materials science. It describes how materials deform under mechanical loading while accounting for thermal expansion, temperature-dependent stiffness, and strain hardening/softening behaviors.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon (proportional stress-strain response)
- Thermo-elastic coupling: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (mechanical strain compensated by thermal expansion)
- Power-law strain hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (plastic deformation regime)
- Exponential saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (asymptotic stress limit)
- Johnson-Cook temperature softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T) (combined hardening and thermal degradation)
- Rational stress saturation: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * epsilon) (bounded nonlinear response)
- Neo-Hookean hyperelasticity (uniaxial): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - epsilon**(-2)) (large deformation elasticity)
- Polynomial thermo-mechanical coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T + c2 * T**2 (higher-order interaction effects)
- Exponential thermal modulus decay: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(-c1 * T) (temperature-dependent stiffness reduction)
- Smooth bilinear elastic-plastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * (epsilon - c2) * (1 - exp(-c3 * epsilon)) (transition from elastic to plastic regime)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic-perfectly plastic transition → Smooth bilinear or piecewise-linear slope changes at yield strain
- Thermal stress compensation → Linear thermal offset (epsilon - c*T) representing thermal expansion counteracting mechanical strain
- Temperature-dependent modulus degradation → Multiplicative softening factors (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) scaling the mechanical stress baseline
- Large deformation geometric nonlinearity → Inverse strain powers (epsilon - epsilon**(-n)) or hyperbolic functions (sinh(c*epsilon)) for finite strain
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to asymptotic stress (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or rational bounds
- Thermo-mechanical cross-coupling → Product interactions (epsilon * T) or (epsilon * exp(-c*T)) capturing temperature-modulated stiffness
- Phase transformation stress response → Sigmoidal or double-well derivative dependence on combined T and epsilon variables

GT symbolic expression: `-c0*(T - c1) + epsilon**c2*c3*(T - c4)`
GT numerical expression: `-0.5449782742323234*(T - 352.1579043725849) + epsilon**0.6261602091724962*1.5180288401497986*(T - 352.1579043725849)`
Let's simplify the GT expression algebraically.
GT = `-c0*T + c0*c1 + c3*epsilon**c2*T - c3*epsilon**c2*c4`
GT = `T * (-c0 + c3*epsilon**c2) + (c0*c1 - c3*c4*epsilon**c2)`
GT = `T * (c3*epsilon**c2 - c0) + (c0*c1 - c3*c4*epsilon**c2)`

Let's look at the structure:
It's a linear function in `T`: `A(epsilon) * T + B(epsilon)`
Where `A(epsilon) = c3 * epsilon**c2 - c0`
And `B(epsilon) = c0*c1 - c3*c4 * epsilon**c2`
Notice that `c1` and `c4` are the same in the GT numerical values: `c1 = 352.1579...`, `c4 = 352.1579...`.
So `B(epsilon) = c0*c1 - c3*c1 * epsilon**c2 = c1 * (c0 - c3 * epsilon**c2) = -c1 * (c3 * epsilon**c2 - c0) = -c1 * A(epsilon)`.
Thus, GT = `A(epsilon) * T - c1 * A(epsilon) = A(epsilon) * (T - c1)`.
This matches the factored form: `(c3*epsilon**c2 - c0) * (T - c1)`.
Wait, the GT is `-c0*(T - c1) + epsilon**c2*c3*(T - c4)`. Since `c1 = c4`, it factors perfectly to `(c3*epsilon**c2 - c0)*(T - c1)`.
So the GT is essentially of the form: `(a * epsilon**b + d) * (T + e)`.
Or expanded: `T * (a * epsilon**b + d) + e * (a * epsilon**b + d)`.
This means the GT is a linear combination of `T` and `1`, with coefficients that are linear combinations of `epsilon**c2` and `1`.
Specifically: `T * (c3*epsilon**c2 - c0) + (c0*c1 - c3*c4*epsilon**c2)`.
Since `c1 = c4`, it's `T * (c3*epsilon**c2 - c0) - c1 * (c3*epsilon**c2 - c0)`.
So the functional form is: `T * (C1 * epsilon**C2 + C3) + (C4 * epsilon**C2 + C5)`.
Actually, it's simpler: `T * (A * epsilon**B + C) + D * (A * epsilon**B + C)`.
Or just `T * (A * epsilon**B + C) + (D * epsilon**B + E)`.

Let's carefully verify Candidate 41 again.
`c0*(T*c1 + c2*(T*c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*epsilon + c6 + c7*epsilon**c4 + c8*epsilon) + c9)`
= `c0*c1*T + c0*c2*c3*T*epsilon**c4 + c0*c2*c5*epsilon + c0*c2*c6 + c0*c2*c7*epsilon**c4 + c0*c2*c8*epsilon + c0*c9`
Group terms:
`T`: `c0*c1`
`T*epsilon**c4`: `c0*c2*c3`
`epsilon**c4`: `c0*c2*c7`
`epsilon`: `c0*c2*(c5+c8)`
`1`: `c0*c2*c6 + c0*c9`
We need to match:
`T`: `-c0_GT`
`T*epsilon**c2_GT`: `c3_GT`
`epsilon**c2_GT`: `-c3_GT*c4_GT`
`1`: `c0_GT*c1_GT`
`epsilon`: `0`
We can set `c4 = c2_GT`.
`c0*c1 = -c0_GT`
`c0*c2*c3 = c3_GT`
`c0*c2*c7 = -c3_GT*c4_GT`
`c0*c2*c6 + c0*c9 = c0_GT*c1_GT`
`c0*c2*(c5+c8) = 0`
We have many free constants. We can easily satisfy these. For example, set `c0=1`, `c1=-c0_GT`, `c2=1`, `c3=c3_GT`, `c7=-c3_GT*c4_GT`, `c6=0`, `c9=c0_GT*c1_GT`, `c5=0`, `c8=0`.
Works perfectly.

Is there any constraint that says we cannot zero out terms? "Zeroing Constants: If a candidate has extra unwanted terms (e.g., an explicit time dependence t when GT is static), you can set their coefficients to 0 to eliminate them." This explicitly allows it.

One minor point: Candidate 41 has `c0*(...)`. If `c0=0`, everything vanishes. But we set `c0=1` or similar non-zero value to match coefficients. That's fine.

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`GT = -c0*(T - c1) + epsilon**c2*c3*(T - c4)`
Given the numerical values, `c1 = c4 = 352.1579...`. Factoring out `(T - c1)`:
`GT = (c3*epsilon**c2 - c0) * (T - c1)`
Expanding this gives the exact functional form:
`GT = T*(c3*epsilon**c2 - c0) + (c0*c1 - c3*c1*epsilon**c2)`
`GT = T*(c3*epsilon**c2) - c0*T - c3*c1*epsilon**c2 + c0*c1`
The GT is a linear combination of exactly four basis functions:
1. `T * epsilon**p` (where `p = c2_GT ≈ 0.626`)
2. `T`
3. `epsilon**p`
4. `1` (constant)

Any candidate that can independently represent these four basis functions (and optionally zero out extra terms like `epsilon`, `exp(...)`, `cos(...)`, etc.) is a `[MATCH]`. Candidates missing any of these four basis functions, or containing non-removable terms like `1/T`, are `[NO MATCH]`.
